# Changelog

All notable changes to this project will be documented in this file.

The English section comes first, followed by a Japanese translation.
The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/), and this project adheres to [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).

## English

### [Unreleased]

#### Added
- **`outline` now hints when a C# file likely uses top-level statements** — When `cdidx outline <path>` targets a non-trivial C# file (`TotalLines >= 20`) that has no `class` / `struct` / `interface` / `enum` / `namespace` / `delegate` / `record` declarations and its file-scope content still contains executable code after skipping `using` / `global using` lines, `[assembly:]` / `[module:]` metadata attributes, comments, and preprocessor directives, the human-readable output now appends a short stderr note explaining that the executable body is represented as top-level statements and therefore is not indexed as outline symbols. This keeps the note off metadata-only files such as `GlobalUsings.cs`, generated `GlobalUsings.g.cs`, and `AssemblyInfo.cs`. JSON output is unchanged so machine consumers that already rely on `OutlineResult` keep their contract. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`.
- **`hotspots --group-by-name` collapses same-name rows across files** — `cdidx hotspots` previously emitted one row per definition site, so same-named helpers in different files (e.g. a shared `InsertIndexedFile` defined in three test files) produced three consecutive rows with the same `reference_count`. The new `--group-by-name` opt-in flag collapses rows that share `(name, kind)` into a single representative row, showing the chosen definition site plus a `(×N sites)` marker in human output, and `definition_sites` / `paths` / `grouped_by="name_kind"` / `definition_site_total` fields in JSON output, including zero-result and `--count --json` payloads. Default behavior is unchanged so existing consumers that want every definition site keep their contract. Help text, README, and regression tests now pin the new option, `hotspots --count`, and the grouped JSON payload shape. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ConsoleUi.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ConsoleUiTests.cs`, `README.md`.
- **Known-file substring finder for CLI and MCP (#128)** — Added `cdidx find <query> --path <pattern>` for literal substring navigation inside already-known indexed files, returning match line/column plus short surrounding context and supporting case-sensitive `--exact`, `--before`, `--after`, `--count`, and JSON output that is easy to chain into `excerpt`. Added matching MCP read-only tool `find_in_file` so AI clients can perform the same focused in-file navigation without falling back to raw-text tools. Updated help, docs, and regression coverage for CLI, DB reader, MCP, and usage text. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ConsoleUi.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Program.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpServer.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolDefinitions.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Models/QueryResults.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ConsoleUiTests.cs`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `CLAUDE.md`. Closes #128.
- **Bundle-level exact-zero hint for `inspect` / `analyze_symbol` (#99)** — `inspect --exact` and MCP `analyze_symbol` now emit a single `exact_zero_hint` when the whole exact bundle comes back empty (definitions, references, callers, and callees all zero) but a relaxed symbol-name probe would have found similarly named symbols. This preserves the one-round-trip contract of the bundled workflow: AI clients can distinguish "true no such symbol" from "exact miss, try the indexed name" without falling back to separate `symbols` calls. CLI human-readable `inspect` now prints the same exact-miss hint text as the leaf commands, CLI JSON includes the new bundle-level field, and MCP `analyze_symbol` adds the same snake_case payload plus a short "Substring would return N..." summary suffix. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSymbolReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Models/QueryResults.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`, `README.md`. Closes #99.
- **`backfill-fold` CLI command and `backfill_fold` MCP tool (#95)** — Add a no-reparse upgrade path for Unicode `--exact` matching on legacy indexes. The new `cdidx backfill-fold [--db <path>] [--json]` command (and matching MCP write tool `backfill_fold`) recomputes `symbols.name_folded` plus `symbol_references.symbol_name_folded` / `container_name_folded` directly from existing DB rows, verifies that no required folded values remain NULL, and stamps `FoldReadyFlag` on success. When fold metadata (`fold_key_version` or `fold_key_fingerprint`) is missing or mismatched, the command rewrites every persisted folded key instead of only NULL rows so version bumps or runtime fold drift cannot silently restamp stale keys. This avoids forcing a full source reparse just to upgrade Unicode-aware exact matching. Status/help/warnings now point users at `backfill-fold` before recommending `cdidx index . --rebuild`. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbWriter.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpServer.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolDefinitions.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ConsoleUi.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Models/QueryResults.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/IndexCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ConsoleUiTests.cs`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #95.
- **Exact-zero hint for `symbols` / `definition` / `references` / `callers` / `callees` (#88)** — When `--exact` returns zero results, the five exact-match commands now automatically rerun the same query without `--exact` and emit an additive `exact_zero_hint` only when relaxed matching would have produced results. CLI human output now explains that `--exact` is the reason the result set is empty and shows up to five sample indexed names, while non-`--count` streaming CLI `--json` keeps zero-hit stdout silent so row-streaming clients can still treat EOF as "no rows." Count/summarize-style JSON paths return a single object, and MCP `structuredContent` mirrors the same `exact_zero_hint` contract for `symbols`, `definition`, `references`, `callers`, and `callees`, with snake_case nested fields (`relaxed_count`, `sample_names`, `suggestion`). The suggestion text was updated to say "exact indexed name" rather than "exact indexed casing" because #86 already made `--exact` Unicode case-insensitive; the remaining failure mode is wrong spelling or over-broad substring intent, not casing drift. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Models/QueryResults.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`. Closes #88.

#### Changed
- **Developer Guide now distinguishes SQLite's role from "zero dependencies" and labels release numbers as examples** — Clarified that cdidx remains a zero-configuration, single-file CLI with exactly one production dependency (`Microsoft.Data.Sqlite`), and made the release-workflow checklist explicitly state that `1.9.0` is only an example version to substitute during an actual release. Affected: `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`.

#### Fixed
- **C# / Java constructor chain calls `: this(...)` / `: base(...)` / `super(...)` now show up as references (#257)** — `ReferenceExtractor` now rewrites C# constructor initializer chains and the equivalent Java constructor-body statements into `call` references pointing at the real target: `: this(args)` / `this(args);` resolves to the enclosing class or record, while `: base(args)` / `super(args);` parses the base type from the enclosing class signature (stripping generics, record primary-ctor args, `where` constraints, `global::` / dotted namespace qualifiers, and ignoring trailing interface entries in the base list). Cross-line C# initializers are attributed to the owning constructor rather than the enclosing class, C# records with `Parent(Value)` primary-ctor chaining get a synthetic function-kind container named after the record so the base call is attributed to the record itself instead of no container at all — the synthetic container now spans the full record declaration header up to the first `;` or `{`, so continuation-line forms like `public record Child(int Value, int Extra)\n    : Parent(Value);` attribute the base call to the record instead of leaving it in no container. Base-type parsing on both languages now uses a depth-aware scanner that splits on `.` / `::` at generic depth 0 and returns the terminal segment, so nested types under generic outer types such as `Outer<int>.Base` (C#), `Outer<Integer>.Base` (Java), and `global::Ns.Outer<T>.Inner` now resolve to `Base` / `Inner` instead of being misattributed to `Outer` and silently mis-aimed in `callers` / `callees` / `impact`. C# `: base(...)` resolution now reconstructs the full enclosing type header from structural lines (reusing the record primary-ctor header helper) instead of trusting `SymbolRecord.Signature`, which only captures the first declaration line, so formatter-style multi-line base-lists such as `class Child\n    : Parent`, `class Child<T>\n    : Outer<T>.Base`, and `class Child<T>\n    : Parent<T>\n    where T : class, new()` no longer silently drop the chain edge. Java `super(...)` resolution mirrors the same reconstruction, so multi-line `extends` forms such as `class Leaf\n    extends Base { Leaf(){super(0);} }`, `class Leaf\n    extends Outer<Integer>.Base {...}`, and `sealed class Leaf\n    extends Base\n    permits None` no longer drop the chain edge either. Java 17+ sealed-type declarations are supported too: the Java base-type scanner now treats `permits` as a word-boundary terminator alongside `implements`, so `sealed class Leaf extends Base permits A, B { Leaf(){super(0);} }` and `extends Outer<Integer>.Base permits A` resolve to `Base` instead of greedily absorbing `permits` into the returned type. Java package-private constructors that SymbolExtractor records without body ranges are found by a name-based fallback against the enclosing class so `Leaf(int x){super(x);}` still attributes the chain edge to the `Leaf` constructor, Java same-line ctor bodies such as `Leaf(int x){super(x);}` / `Leaf(){this(0);}` (which SymbolExtractor skips because the line ends with `}` instead of `{`/`,`/`;`) are handled by relaxing the ctor-chain regex to also match after `{` and by synthesizing a ctor container directly from the declaration line. The declaration-line scanner is depth-aware so it accepts fully qualified annotations with optional nested-paren argument lists (e.g. `@demo.Ann Leaf(int x){super(x);}`, `@SuppressWarnings({"unused", "unchecked"}) Leaf(...)`) and nested generic bounds on ctor type parameters (e.g. `public <T extends Comparable<Integer>> Leaf(T x){super(0);}`, `<U extends java.util.List<? extends Number>> Leaf(...)`), so annotated and generic same-line ctors are no longer silently dropped as class-scope phantom edges, and Java `this(...)` is added to the Java ignore set so the generic call scanner does not emit a phantom `call this` edge after the chain is rewritten. Java `super.method()` is still left alone as a regular call. `callers`, `references`, `callees`, and `impact` now surface the missing chain edges so a rename of a base constructor no longer looks safe when every subclass constructor chains to it. Java base-type resolution also strips JLS 9.7.4 type-use annotations before extracting the terminal segment, so `class Leaf extends @Ann Root`, `extends @pkg.Ann(value=1) Root`, `extends @Ann @Other Root`, and `extends Outer<Integer>.@Ann Base` resolve to the real base type instead of a phantom `@Ann Root` / `@Ann Base` name that silently misattributes `super(...)` edges. The base-list scanner also tracks `(...)` depth alongside `<...>` depth so commas inside annotation arguments such as `@Ann(a = 1, b = 2) Root`, `@Ann({A.class, B.class}) Root`, and `@pkg.Ann(value = {1, 2, 3}) Root` are no longer mistaken for top-level base-list separators (which previously truncated the segment before the annotation stripper could run and dropped the `super(...)` edge entirely). Java enums can declare constructors and chain via `this(...)`, so the enclosing-type candidate list and the innermost-class-like lookup now include `enum` alongside `class` / `struct` / `interface`; `enum Shade { Red, Blue(1); Shade(){ this(0); } Shade(int code){} }` now emits the chain edge to the enum instead of being silently dropped (C# enum is a no-op here because it cannot declare constructors and the C# chain regex never matches inside one). Added regression coverage for C# `: this(...)` / `: base(...)` (including generic bases, records attributed to the synthetic constructor, multi-line record continuation-line base calls, braced record bodies after a base call, cross-line wraps, `global::` base types, nested types under generic outer types such as `Outer<int>.Base` and `global::Ns.Outer<T>.Inner`, plain multi-line class base-lists like `class Child\n    : Parent`, multi-line nested-generic base-lists like `class Child<T>\n    : Outer<T>.Base`, and multi-line base-lists followed by `where` constraints) and Java `super(...)` / `this(...)` (including package-private constructors, public and package-private same-line ctor bodies for both `super(...)` and `this(...)`, same-line ctor bodies with leading annotations, same-line ctor bodies with generic type parameters, fully qualified annotations with nested-paren argument lists, nested generic bounds on ctor type parameters, nested types under generic outer types such as `Outer<Integer>.Base`, sealed / non-sealed / `permits`-bearing declarations including `extends Outer<Integer>.Base permits A`, multi-line `extends` base-lists like `class Leaf\n    extends Base`, multi-line `extends Outer<Integer>.Base`, multi-line `extends` with continuation-line `permits`, JLS 9.7.4 type-use annotated `extends` (`extends @Ann Root`, `extends @pkg.Ann Root`, `extends @Ann(value=1) Root`, `extends @Ann @Other Root`, `extends Outer<Integer>.@Ann Base`, `extends @Ann Outer<Integer>.Base`, `extends @Ann Root implements Foo`) including the E2E `super(...)` paths that would have pointed at a phantom annotated type, Java enum `this(...)` constructor chain attribution, and phantom `this` suppression). Java same-line ctor name extraction now accepts `@annotation` and `public` / `protected` / `private` / `static` / `final` / `abstract` modifiers in any order so formatter-style forms like `public @Deprecated Leaf(int x){super(x);}` and `@demo.Ann private Leaf(){this(0);}` no longer silently drop the chain edge when an annotation sits between modifiers instead of before them. The multi-line header collector is also depth-aware in `()` / `[]` / `<>` depth so `{` / `;` inside annotation arguments, array initializers, or generic bounds (e.g. `extends @Ann({A.class, B.class}) Root {`) no longer truncate the enclosing-type header before the real base type; this helper feeds both Java multi-line `extends` resolution and C# record primary-ctor container synthesis. `SymbolExtractor.FindBraceRange` is now also depth-aware in `()` / `[]` so that `{` / `}` inside annotation-argument and attribute-argument braces (`@Ann({A.class, B.class})`, array-initializer arguments, annotation-nested `{}`) do not count as body braces and no longer collapse the enclosing type's body range to a single line. Without that fix, `class Leaf extends @Ann({A.class, B.class}) Root { Leaf() { super(0); } }` would index `Leaf` with a one-line body range, so the `super(0)` call-site fell outside the Leaf class and no ctor body was recognized, silently dropping the `super(...)` chain edge from `callers` / `references` / `impact` even with the depth-aware ReferenceExtractor header collector in place. The same `FindBraceRange` depth tracking now also honors block comments (`/* ... */`), line comments (`//`), string literals (`"..."`), and Rust / OCaml-style lifetime annotations (`'a`, `'static`) separately from real single-character literals (`'x'`, `'\n'`), so unbalanced `(`, `[`, `{`, or `}` tokens living inside comments or strings can no longer break the body range. In parallel, `ReferenceExtractor.CollectCSharpRecordHeader` no longer tracks `<` / `>` as generic depth — which previously reacted to comparison operators such as `[Attr(Flag = 1 < 2)]` and extended the synthetic C# primary-ctor container all the way to EOF, incorrectly attributing body calls after the real `{` to the record ctor — and now masks comment / string / char-literal content to spaces before appending it to the joined header buffer, so `class Leaf extends Root /* ( stray [ */ { ... super(0); ... }`-style headers round-trip cleanly through `ParseCSharpBaseType` / `ParseJavaBaseType` without the masked noise poisoning base-type resolution. Added an E2E regression test that rebuilds both SymbolExtractor symbols and ReferenceExtractor edges for a brace-annotation `extends` fixture and asserts the `Root` call lands inside the Leaf ctor body, plus a `CollectCSharpRecordHeader` comparison-operator regression test and an E2E C# primary-ctor regression test that locks the attribute-argument comparison operator and comment / string noise cases against header-scoped container synthesis. Added regression coverage for Java same-line modifier-before-annotation ctors and for the depth-aware header collector directly. C# record primary-ctor container synthesis no longer relies on a first-line regex over `SymbolRecord.Signature` for gating: the stored signature only captures the first declaration line, so split-line forms like `public record Child\n(\n    int Value\n)\n    : Parent(Value);` were silently excluded and the `Parent(Value)` edge collapsed onto class/no-container instead of the synthetic record ctor. The gate now runs on the joined multi-line header produced by `CollectCSharpRecordHeader`, so split-line record primary-ctors with multi-line `: base(...)` continuations also attribute the chain edge to the synthetic function-kind container named after the record; added a direct regression test covering that split-line shape. The synthetic record-ctor container is also applied at call-site granularity rather than line-level: `CollectCSharpRecordHeader` now reports the terminator column on the end line, and the override only replaces the container for call-site matches whose column sits inside the header span. Without this scoping, legal same-line bodies like `record Child(int V) : Parent(V) { public int Sum() => Add(V, 1); }` silently handed `Add(...)` to the synthetic record ctor even though it lives past the header-terminating `{` and belongs to a real body-level container, polluting `callers` / `impact` with phantom record-ctor callers. The record-header detector now also tracks generic / bracket depth when looking for the primary-ctor `(` in the first base-list entry so that tuple-type interface implementations such as `record Pair(int A, int B) : IBox<(int Left, int Right)>` (where `(` appears inside `<...>`) are no longer mistaken for a primary-ctor base call, which previously synthesized a phantom record-ctor container over the whole declaration line and misattributed unrelated body calls. Synthetic primary-ctor container generation has also been generalized from C# records to C# 12 `class` and `struct` primary constructors: `public class Child(int value) : Parent(value)`, the split-line form `public class ChildSplit\n(\n    int value\n) : Parent(\n    value\n)`, generic forms like `public class GenericChild<T>(T value) : Parent(42)`, same-line braced bodies like `public class ChildWithBody(int value) : Parent(value) { public int Doubled { get; } = Helper.Compute(value); }`, and struct primary ctors like `public struct BoxedValue(int value) : BaseImpl(value)` now all attribute the base-list primary-ctor call to a synthetic `function`-kind container named after the enclosing type instead of collapsing onto the class itself or no container at all. The header-end column scoping still applies so body calls past the header-terminating `{` stay attributed to their real inner container. Added regression coverage for the same-line braced-body and tuple-in-base-list record shapes as well as class (same-line, split-line, generic, same-line braced body) and struct C# 12 primary-ctor shapes. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #257.
- **C# enum members now index as `enum` symbols without breaking compact-body flows (#214)** — C# enum member extraction now keeps enum values out of the generic `function` bucket, recognizes lowercase / Unicode-start identifiers such as `active` and `Δelta`, keeps enum-member ownership intact for compact same-line bodies, same-line sibling enum declarations, and same-line nested namespace/class containers, and recovers member extraction after incomplete member attributes such as `[Attr(`. `unused` now excludes only C# enum members, while active scopes containing C# enums still surface degraded graph metadata because enum declarations can remain false positives until container-aware enum-member access edges exist. Those scopes now expose explicit `unsupported_symbol_kind=enum_member` metadata across `inspect`, exact `references` / `callers` / `callees`, and `unused` instead of silently treating empty or mixed graph results as authoritative; exact zero-hit graph JSON always emits a machine-readable payload, and mixed exact graph hits now keep `graph_language` / `graph_supported` aligned with the actual graph-capable definition even without `--lang`. Mixed-name inspect bundles now keep `graph_supported` aligned with callable candidates while still flagging the enum-member gap, exact graph-limit detection now uses existence checks rather than a capped definition list, and successful exact CLI/MCP graph rows carry the same degradation metadata as zero/count payloads. Added extractor, outline, CLI, and MCP regression coverage for the compact-body, incomplete-attribute, exact zero-hit, and enum-member graph-limit paths, plus negative graph coverage so unresolved qualified accesses like `Nested.A` or non-enum `Values.A` do not get indexed as bare enum-member references prematurely. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSymbolReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #214.
- **CSS `@font-face` family extraction now ignores `font-family:` text inside unquoted data URLs** — The CSS masking pass now blanks `url(...)` payloads while still tracking nested parentheses, so `@font-face` family-name extraction no longer mistakes unquoted `data:` URLs such as `url(data:...;font-family:bogus)` for the real declaration. This also keeps brace-based selector context from being polluted by `{}` embedded inside SVG data URLs. Added regression coverage for unquoted data URLs and SVG data URLs. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`.
- **C# expression-bodied and block-bodied property callers attribute to the individual method/property instead of the enclosing class (#233)** — `SymbolExtractor` now detects `=> expr;` at top level inside `FindCSharpBraceRange` and assigns a body range covering the declaration line through the terminating `;` (including the multi-line form where `=>` is placed on a following indented line, both for methods and for expression-bodied properties). The block-bodied property scanner now also merges the common Microsoft-style `public int Wrap {` + next-line `get { ... }` shape with its accessor line so that form is recognized alongside the existing K&R (`public int Wrap { get { ... } }`) and Allman (`public int Wrap` then `{` on the next line) shapes, without misclassifying `public class X {` or other non-property headers. Block comments spanning several lines between the header and the body are handled correctly by the same line-scanning path. `ReferenceExtractor.FindInnermostContainer` now accepts `property` as a container kind alongside `function` / `class` / `namespace`. As a result `callers <Target>`, `impact_analysis`, and the caller rows surfaced by `inspect` / `analyze_symbol` no longer collapse `public int Wrap() => Compute();`, `public int Wrap => Compute();`, the block-bodied `public int Wrap { get { return Compute(); } }` (K&R), `public int Wrap {` / `    get { return Compute(); }` / `}` (same-line brace with next-line accessor), the Allman-style `public int Wrap` / `{` / `    get { return Compute(); }` / `}`, the multi-line expression-bodied `public int Wrap` / `    => Compute();`, or the same shapes with multi-line block comments between header and body into a single enclosing-class row — each caller now appears on its own row with the correct `caller_kind` (`function` or `property`) and `caller_name`. Regression coverage spans symbol body ranges, all three block-bodied property shapes plus a misclassification guard for bare-brace lines whose body is not an accessor, accessor-attribute and visibility-prefixed accessor lines, reference attribution for expression-bodied methods / properties / multi-line `=> expr;` / K&R block-bodied accessor / bare-brace-same-line accessor-next-line / Allman-style / multi-line expression-bodied property forms, the block-comment-between-header-and-body variants for both Allman and multi-line expression-bodied properties, the previously-encoded ternary-continuation caller test, and end-to-end `callers` assertions through the CLI for the K&R shape (covered by existing property tests), the bare-brace-same-line shape, the Allman block-body shape, the multi-line expression-bodied shape, and both block-comment-separated variants. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #233.
- **C# 13 partial properties now participate in symbol extraction (#228)** — The C# extractor now accepts the `partial` modifier on properties and looks ahead across multiline headers, so brace-on-next-line declarations, block-bodied implementations, multiline expression-bodied properties, and `partial override` forms no longer disappear from `symbols`, `definition`, `outline`, `hotspots`, and related symbol-driven commands. Added regression coverage for multiline declaration-style, block-bodied implementation, and multiline `partial override` properties. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #228.
- **C# operators, conversion operators, and indexers now use navigable symbol names (#213)** — `SymbolExtractor` now stores overloads as names like `operator +` and `operator checked +`, stores `implicit` / `explicit` conversion operators as exact names like `implicit operator decimal`, `explicit operator Money`, `explicit operator Dictionary<string, int>`, and `explicit operator (int whole, int cents)` so they no longer collide with constructors, and normalizes C# indexers from the keyword `this` to the CLR-style name `Item`. Tuple/generic conversion target types now go through a lightweight type scanner and canonical whitespace normalization, including named tuple elements after generic, array, nested-tuple, nullable type tokens, `unsafe` pointer targets, and function-pointer target types, so exact-name queries do not depend on the source file's spacing style. Incremental `cdidx index .` now tracks a C# symbol-name contract version in `codeindex_meta` and automatically re-extracts unchanged C# files once when a canonical-name upgrade lands, so existing DBs pick up the new exact names without requiring `--rebuild`; `status` also exposes `csharp_symbol_name_ready`, exact-name queries surface stale canonical-name degradation instead of silent false negatives, `status --db ...` now prints a repair command that targets the diagnosed DB instead of the caller's default workspace DB, and MCP exact-name trust metadata now honors the active query scope instead of degrading unrelated languages or paths. Added regression coverage in extractor, DB query, CLI query, MCP query, status, and index-upgrade tests, and updated the developer guide and README to document the naming convention. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbContext.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbWriter.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Models/QueryResults.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/IndexCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `README.md`. Closes #213.
- **C# events and delegates with spaced generic types no longer misparse under bogus names (#223)** — The dedicated C# `event` and `delegate` extractor patterns now accept formatter-style spaces inside generic type tokens and anchor the event name against real declaration terminators. This fixes `event Action<string, int> NamedEvent;` / `event Func<string, int, bool> Filter;` being indexed as `event int`, and restores dropped delegates such as `delegate Task<Dictionary<string, int>> LoadAsync();`. Added regression coverage for multi-argument generic events, generic delegates, and the existing single-token forms. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #223.
- **C# members with spaced generic type tokens no longer disappear from symbol extraction (#222)** — The C# extractor now accepts spaces inside generic type tokens for method return types, explicit-interface implementations, properties, indexers, delegates, and events, so idiomatic signatures such as `Task<Result<A, B>>`, `Dictionary<K, V>`, and `Action<T1, T2>` no longer vanish or misparse just because Roslyn-style formatting inserts a space after commas. Added regression coverage for nested generic return types, tuple returns, explicit-interface methods, properties, indexers, delegates, and events. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #222.
- **C# targeted attribute declarations no longer become phantom top-level functions (#219)** — The C# symbol extractor now strips whole-line attribute lists all the way to empty output, and its general method regex explicitly rejects targeted-attribute prefixes such as `[assembly:]`, `[module:]`, `[return:]`, and `[param:]`. This prevents assembly/module attributes like `CLSCompliant`, `AssemblyVersion`, and `SkipLocalsInit` from polluting `symbols`, `definition`, `hotspots`, `unused`, and `map` as fake `function` definitions. Regression coverage also locks in that `[return: MarshalAs(...)]` still contributes a normal `call` reference, so targeted attributes round-trip through `references` the same way as non-target attributes. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #219.
- **Reference extraction no longer applies unrelated keyword blacklists across every language (#200)** — `ReferenceExtractor` now keeps a small shared ignore set for truly cross-language syntax words and scopes the larger keyword/builtin filters by language, so Python/JavaScript/Ruby/C# calls like `print()`, `require()`, `run()`, `build()`, `apply()`, and `task.Run()` are no longer silently dropped just because those names are special in Haskell, Makefile, Gradle, R, or other unrelated languages. Added regression coverage for the cross-language false-negative cases reported in #200. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #200.
- **C# symbol extraction now ignores pseudo-code inside raw/verbatim strings and comments** — The C# extraction path now runs the stateful lexer before regex matching, sanitizing raw string literals, verbatim strings, regular strings, chars, and comments so fixture code inside `""" ... """`, `@"..."`, and block comments no longer pollutes `symbols`, `outline`, or dogfooding runs against the repo itself. Added regression coverage for raw-string, verbatim-string, and block-comment pseudo-code. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`.
- **JavaScript / TypeScript control-flow blocks and anonymous-class edge cases no longer corrupt symbol extraction (#154)** — Tightened the JS/TS method-shape extractor so class-body control-flow statements like `if (...) {}`, `for (...) {}`, `while (...) {}`, and `switch (...) {}` are rejected before they can be tagged as `function` symbols, while valid keyword-named methods, same-line modifier-named methods such as `async()` / `static()`, methods with default arguments, computed-name methods, `#private` methods, generator / `async *` methods, regex-literal bodies, wrapped control-flow conditions, default-export classes, anonymous default classes, anonymous `export default abstract class`, top-level and namespace-scoped class expressions, multiline and parenthesized exported/CommonJS class-expression bindings, TypeScript `export = class ...` assignments, same-line sibling classes, statement-prefixed same-line public classes and class expressions after earlier expressions or function bodies, colon-delimited ternary/object-value class expressions staying private, TypeScript generic methods, and same-line TypeScript methods with object / conditional / function-return-object return types still keep correct class ranges, signatures, return-type metadata, and method containers. Top-level and exported class expressions now index under their exported or assigned binding name instead of a private inner class name, statement-prefixed synthetic class-expression signatures are trimmed to the actual declaration start, same-line class bodies can emit multiple sibling methods without inflating the first method signature, same-line sibling classes keep distinct containers even when their method names collide, wrapped and ASI-terminated blockless arrow expressions now keep correct function ranges without swallowing following expression statements or CommonJS class exports, parenthesized and multiline anonymous `export default class` headers plus multiline class-expression assignment headers are recognized, and JS/TS private-scope filtering now covers direct local class declarations plus synthetic class scanning inside class methods, object-literal concise methods/getters/setters, function-expression / IIFE wrappers, blockless arrow-expression bodies, and `static {}` initialization blocks. Normal block-scoped `class` declarations and `const` / `let` class-expression bindings inside `if` / `switch` / `try` blocks are now suppressed as private implementation details, while namespace exports, CommonJS exports, and TypeScript `export =` class exports still remain indexable. Regression tests cover the added JS/TS parser edge cases. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #154.
- **CSS/SCSS symbol extraction now covers modern selectors and design tokens (#211)** — CSS symbol extraction now keeps literal selector names for exact lookup, adds `:root`, custom properties, `%placeholder`, standalone attribute selectors, pseudo selectors, and `@font-face` family names, and skips family-less `@font-face` fallback noise. Grouping at-rules such as `@media` still expose their contained selectors, while true nested selectors remain suppressed. Brace-range handling now stays correct across C#, Rust, CSS, JavaScript, and TypeScript, including JS/TS template literals and `${...}` interpolations, so `outline` and container metadata do not regress on the new selector coverage. Added extractor and CLI regression coverage for CSS exact-name queries plus C#/Rust/JS/TS brace-range edge cases. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #211.
- **Trimmed-release CLI `--json` now fails with a dedicated feature-unavailable signal instead of a fake database error (#147)** — Published self-contained builds still cannot serialize CLI `--json` payloads under `PublishTrimmed=true`, but the observable failure is now truthful: the CLI reports `Error: --json is not available on this trimmed build.`, prints a structured-output hint that points users at MCP / human-readable output / the NuGet tool build, and exits with code `4` (`FeatureUnavailable`) instead of misclassifying the problem as exit code `3` (`DatabaseError`). Added entrypoint regression tests that cover both the DB-backed `status --json` path and the pre-DB `index --json` error path, updated the user/developer docs to describe the current limitation accurately, and taught the release workflow to assert the published binary now returns exit code `4` without the old `database error` wording. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Program.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ProgramRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/JsonOutputFailure.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/CommandExitCodes.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ProgramRunnerTests.cs`, `.github/workflows/release.yml`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `CLOUD_BOOTSTRAP_PROMPT.md`, `CLAUDE.md`. Closes #147.
- **Unknown-command suggestions no longer over-match short inputs** — `FindClosestCommand` now uses Damerau-Levenshtein distance with a length-aware threshold so short unknown commands are no longer steered toward unrelated longer commands (for example `fold` no longer suggests `find` just because it is within the old global distance-3 cutoff), while common typos and missing hyphens such as `serach` and `backfillfold` still resolve to the intended command. Added regression coverage for the tighter heuristic. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ConsoleUi.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ConsoleUiTests.cs`.
- **Explicit root paths now bypass descendant skip-dir filters (#153)** — `FileIndexer.ScanFiles()` no longer applies the default skip-directory list to the project root itself, so commands like `cdidx node_modules`, `cdidx vendor`, `cdidx target`, or `cdidx .` from inside those directories no longer silently produce empty indexes. Descendant skip behavior is unchanged, and regression tests now cover explicit roots whose leaf names match `SkipDirs`. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`. Closes #153.
- **Release verify step waits for CDN-propagated download URL and `gh release create` is idempotent** — The `Verify install.sh against the published release` step in `.github/workflows/release.yml` previously called `install.sh` immediately after `gh release create`, which races the GitHub release download CDN. Asset URLs returned 404 for several seconds even though the API listed them, making the v1.10.0 release run fail despite the actual release being healthy. Added a preceding `Wait for release assets to be downloadable` step that polls the public `releases/download/<tag>/CodeIndex-linux-x64.tar.gz` URL with up to ten 5-second retries before the verify step runs. Also made `Create GitHub release` idempotent: when the same-tag release already exists (e.g. on a re-run after a transient verify failure), the step now uploads any missing assets via `gh release upload --clobber` instead of failing with `a release with the same tag name already exists`. Affected: `.github/workflows/release.yml`.
- **Added regression coverage for existing C# 11 checked-operator extraction (#238)** — The runtime fix for C# 11 user-defined `operator checked` overloads and `explicit operator checked ...` conversion operators already shipped in earlier commits on main, but there was no dedicated regression test pinning the concrete fixture from the bug report, so the issue could not be closed cleanly. Added a dedicated `SymbolExtractor` regression test that locks the issue's repro (unchecked + checked pairs for binary `+`, binary `-`, unary `-`, and `explicit operator int` / `explicit operator checked int`) under distinct symbol names (`operator +` vs `operator checked +`, `explicit operator int` vs `explicit operator checked int`), so AI clients can disambiguate the two overloads in `symbols`, `definition`, `callers`, and `inspect`. Also updated the developer guide's C# language-pattern row to call out `operator checked -` and `explicit operator checked int` alongside the existing `operator checked +` and `explicit operator checked byte` examples. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #238.
- **Added regression coverage for C# multi-line raw/verbatim string reference masking (#288)** — The runtime fix for phantom `call` reference edges sitting inside C# multi-line raw strings (`""" ... """`), verbatim strings (`@" ... "`), and interpolated raw strings (`$""" ... """`) already shipped with #177's `StructuralLineMasker`, but `ReferenceExtractorTests` only locked the single raw-string fixture and the single-line escaped-brace case, so the exact repro from the bug report (multi-line verbatim body with `BadCall()`, plus the combined raw / interpolated raw / verbatim body with `EvilCall`, `AnotherCall`, `PhantomCall`, and `BadCall`) could not be closed cleanly. Added two dedicated regression tests that pin the multi-line `@"..."` body and the full combined issue repro end-to-end through `SymbolExtractor` + `ReferenceExtractor`, asserting that every call-looking identifier inside the string bodies is suppressed while the real `RealCall()` after the strings is still captured with the correct container. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #288.
- **C# methods, properties, indexers, delegates, and explicit-interface implementations with pointer / function-pointer return types are no longer dropped from symbol extraction (#234)** — `SymbolExtractor` now accepts `*` in the shared C# return-type character class and relaxes the `delegate`-keyword negative lookahead so `delegate*<...>` passes through, while `delegate Foo Bar()` style named delegate declarations continue to be handled by their dedicated pattern. The explicit-interface return-type regex has been consolidated onto the same `CSharpTypePattern`, so nested function-pointer payloads such as `delegate*<List<int>, int> IFoo.Transform()`, `delegate*<delegate*<int, void>, int> IFoo.TransformFp()`, and `delegate* unmanaged[Cdecl]<List<int>, int> IFoo.TransformUnmanaged()` are handled uniformly with the regular method / property / indexer / delegate paths instead of tripping on the first nested `>`. Methods such as `int* Get(...)`, `void** Double()`, `byte* Get1()`, `delegate*<int, int> Transform()`, and `int*[] Arr()` are now indexed with `ReturnType` preserved, and the same fix naturally covers pointer properties (`int* P { get; set; }`, `byte* Q => null`), pointer indexers (`int* this[int i]`), delegate declarations with pointer returns (`public unsafe delegate int* PointerDelegate(int)`), and explicit-interface implementations like `int* IFoo.Get()` and `delegate*<int, int> IFoo.Transform()`. Added regression coverage for each form, including nested generics inside `delegate*<...>` payloads and `delegate* unmanaged[Cdecl]<...>` calling conventions, to lock the behavior in place. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #234.
- **C# `ref` / `ref readonly` return members are no longer dropped from symbol extraction (#224)** — C# method, property, expression-bodied property, dedicated indexer, and explicit-interface-implementation patterns now accept `ref` and `ref readonly` return modifiers before the return type, so APIs such as `public ref int Value`, `public ref readonly int this[int i]`, and `ref int IFoo.GetRef()` are indexed instead of silently disappearing. Regression coverage now locks the extracted names for ref-return methods, properties, indexers, explicit interface implementations, and confirms existing `readonly struct` / `ref struct` detection still works. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #224.
- **Indexing now honors `.gitignore` and `.cdidxignore` across full and scoped refreshes (#201)** — `FileIndexer` keeps the existing hardcoded skip lists for non-repo junk/build output, then layers user `.gitignore` and optional `.cdidxignore` rules with last-match-wins negation. The same path filter is now reused by full scans, `--files`, and `--commits` updates, so explicitly refreshed ignored files are deleted instead of re-indexed. When ignore files themselves are refreshed, cdidx falls back to a full scan so newly ignored files are purged safely. Git-managed workspaces now also follow the repository's `core.ignorecase` setting instead of assuming an OS-wide policy, even when the indexed project root is a subdirectory inside that repo; that matching now folds ASCII only, matching Git's non-ASCII behavior more closely. Ancestor `.gitignore` files above that subdirectory are preloaded, directory-level ancestor rules can now exclude the indexed project root itself, and both `--commits` and relevant ancestor `--files` inputs normalize Git's repository-root-relative paths back to the indexed project root before filtering them. Built-in skip directories still apply to descendants, but an explicitly requested `projectPath` itself remains indexable regardless of basename. `**` is only treated specially in Git's path-form globstar cases rather than as an unrestricted cross-directory wildcard, and POSIX bracket classes now follow Git's ASCII wildmatch behavior instead of Unicode categories. Malformed ignore lines, including truncated bracket classes that Git would reject, are surfaced as warnings without degrading readiness, while unreadable ignore files still fail closed for that directory scope instead of indexing with incomplete rules; scoped updates that hit unreadable ignore rules now conservatively demote readiness instead of advertising the index as authoritative. Regression tests now cover exact-file, directory, glob, negation, nested `.gitignore`, `.cdidxignore`, bracket classes, POSIX classes, escapes, malformed and unreadable ignore handling, ignore-case config, subdirectory repo roots, ancestor ignore rules, project-root directory excludes, non-special `**`, and update-mode behavior. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/GitHelper.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/IndexCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/GitHelperTests.cs`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`. Closes #201.
- **C# and Java record primary components now surface as symbols (#220)** — `SymbolExtractor` now emits synthetic `property` symbols for C# positional-record components and Java record components, so `symbols` / `definition` / `outline` no longer treat `record Point(int X, int Y)` or `record Point(int x, int y)` as memberless shells. The extractor handles generic records, inheritance clauses, body-member coexistence, long wrapped component lists, and comment-bearing component declarations, and the language-pattern reference table now documents the new property coverage. Added regression coverage for C# record classes/structs and Java records. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #220.
- **`install.sh` now stays truthful about latest installs and failure recovery (#185)** — The installer still detects an existing `cdidx` binary before download, but no-argument reruns once again target the latest published release instead of silently pinning the current local version forever. A healthy existing install now skips only after the installer resolves `/releases/latest` and confirms the installed version already matches that latest tag; older healthy installs upgrade normally, while broken `v0.0.0`, same-version incomplete installs, or installs missing required adjacent assets are treated as reinstall targets. Explicit target versions continue to force reinstall/switch handling even when the same healthy version is already installed. Latest-release parsing now prefers `jq` when available and falls back to the existing `grep` + `sed` pipeline for portability, curl/HTTP failures are classified as rate-limit / HTTP / real network errors instead of the old generic “Check your network connection” message, download errors now carry HTTP-specific guidance too, missing checksum entries in `sha256sums.txt` now raise the intended actionable installer error instead of failing silently under `pipefail`, and version-change logs now say `Switching` instead of incorrectly claiming every non-equal install is an upgrade. Payload validation now happens before any promotion, staged files are swapped into `INSTALL_DIR` with runtime assets first and the binary last, backup/promotion move failures roll back only the files touched in that phase, rollback preserves recovery artifacts if rollback itself fails, and rollback restores the previous install instead of deleting untouched old assets. Added Unix-only installer regression coverage plus documentation updates for latest-target semantics, staged writes, rollback safety, mktemp handling, and macOS asset paths. Affected: `install.sh`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/InstallScriptTests.cs`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`. Closes #185.
- **`--count` now returns true totals instead of `min(total, limit)` (#159)** — `search`, `symbols`, `definition`, `references`, `callers`, `callees`, `files`, and `find` previously reused their paged result readers for count-only mode, so the reported `count` silently flattened to the default page size or an explicit `--limit`. Count-only CLI paths now use dedicated unbounded count queries that preserve each command's real result semantics, including search-result deduplication, logical graph row grouping, and find's per-occurrence counting, while still reporting matching file counts where applicable. README and regression tests now pin that `--count` ignores `--limit` for preflight checks. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSearchReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSymbolReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Models/QueryResults.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `README.md`. Closes #159.
- **Large-index `hotspots` / `deps` graph aggregates no longer blow SQLite temp-store on duplicate-heavy names (#179)** — `GetSymbolHotspots`, `GetGroupedSymbolHotspots`, and `GetFileDependencies` now aggregate logical reference-site counts before joining them back to symbol/file metadata, replacing the old per-reference × per-symbol join shape that could trigger `SQLite Error 13: 'database or disk is full'` on Roslyn-sized indexes. `deps` now also keeps target hydration language-scoped so `--lang csharp` edges do not accidentally join same-named symbols from other languages. CLI query execution now detects `SQLITE_FULL` specifically and prints a temp-store exhaustion hint instead of the generic stale/corrupt DB advice. Added regression coverage for same-language dependency matching and grouped hotspot aggregation over duplicate names. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSymbolReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #179.
- **Extensionless shebang scripts are now indexed under their inferred language (#158)** — `FileIndexer` no longer limits indexability to known extensions and exact filename matches. When those checks miss, it now reads the first line and recognizes common shebang interpreters so extensionless scripts under directories like `libexec/` still enter the index as `shell`, `python`, `ruby`, `javascript`, `php`, `lua`, or `powershell`. The fallback stays limited to truly extensionless files, only accepts real first-column shebangs (BOM allowed, leading spaces/tabs rejected), full-scan/update-mode refreshes now purge previously indexed rows when those files lose their shebang and become non-indexable, unreadable paths now degrade the run to partial instead of deleting existing indexed rows or advertising the index as fully ready, and scan/probe failures now report actionable file or directory paths in partial-run errors. Update mode now demotes readiness for any target file that fails probe/read/build, including newly added files, so partial scoped refreshes cannot leave the DB advertised as fully ready. Partial full scans now retain subtree-level scan coverage so they still purge positively observed non-indexable files everywhere plus stale deleted files whose immediate parent directory completed its own file listing successfully even when another subtree or descendant is unreadable, and the human purge message now explicitly scopes that branch to “positively observed as no longer indexable” and “missing from directories whose file listing completed successfully.” `--dry-run` mirrors the same regular-file/readability/scan-failure/outside-root filtering as real indexing instead of overcounting FIFOs, unreadable files, unreadable subtrees, or files outside the project root. Unix special files (for example FIFOs named `tool`, `tool.sh`, or `Dockerfile`) are skipped before any read/probe path can block indexing. Added regression coverage for language detection, directory scanning, full-scan/update-mode purge behavior, unreadable-path handling, FIFO handling, and `BuildRecord`, and updated user/developer docs to document the shebang fallback plus the full PowerShell extension set. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbWriter.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/IndexCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `CLAUDE.md`. Closes #158.
- **C# raw-string fixture contents no longer leak phantom symbols or references (#177)** — Structural extraction now masks C# raw string literal bodies before line-based regex matching, so embedded fixture code like `public class App` or `function main()` no longer appears as real C# symbols, no longer pollutes `map` entrypoints, and no longer contributes phantom C# call edges. The masking pass now also handles nested string forms inside interpolated raw-string holes, including nested interpolated strings like `$"{Run()}"` and nested raw-string arguments like `Id(""" ... """)`, so real call edges survive while fixture text inside those nested strings stays masked. Interpolated regular and verbatim strings now also treat `{{` and `}}` as escaped literal braces instead of interpolation delimiters, preventing phantom references like `$@"{{Run()}}"` and phantom symbols leaking from multi-line escaped-brace fixture text. Added regression coverage for symbol extraction, reference extraction, and `map --json` entrypoint output, including the nested interpolation and escaped-brace cases. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/StructuralLineMasker.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #177.
- **C# switch-expression arms no longer become phantom properties (#208)** — `SymbolExtractor` now precomputes which lines are inside a C# `switch { ... }` expression region and rejects expression-bodied property matches only in that context, instead of tightening visibility rules across all C# members. This removes bogus `property` rows for type-pattern arms such as `int neg => ...` and keeps mixed constant-pattern arms from polluting symbol listings, while real expression-bodied properties continue to index normally. Added regression coverage using the reported mixed type-pattern and constant-pattern fixture and verified the local built `cdidx.dll` now returns only the class and methods from that file. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #208.
- **Graph queries now collapse duplicate constructor `call` + `instantiate` sites and document `--kind` semantics (#176)** — Default `references`, `callers`, `callees`, transitive caller traversal, `deps`, and `hotspots` counting now deduplicate constructor sites that were previously stored twice at the same `file:line:column`, so ctor-heavy classes no longer look 2x more referenced than they really are unless the caller explicitly filters by `--kind call` or `--kind instantiate`. Default graph queries still keep non-constructor kinds such as `subscribe` visible, so event-subscription rows continue to appear in `references`, `callers`, `callees`, `inspect`, and MCP `analyze_symbol` bundles unless the caller explicitly filters them away. CLI help/README/MCP docs now spell out that `--kind` means symbol kind on symbol-oriented commands but reference kind on graph commands, and human-readable graph queries warn when a symbol kind such as `class` is passed to `references`/`callers`/`callees`. Added regression coverage for deduplicated constructor-site counts, default `subscribe` visibility, and the new warning/help text. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSymbolReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ConsoleUi.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolDefinitions.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ConsoleUiTests.cs`, `README.md`. Closes #176.
- **C# ternary continuation calls no longer become phantom method definitions (#175)** — The C# method-with-return-type regex now rejects lines whose first non-whitespace token is `?` or `:`, so multi-line ternary branches like `? RunUpdateMode(...)` and `: RunFullScan(...)` are no longer indexed as fake method declarations. This removes duplicate phantom symbols, lets the reference extractor keep the real call edge, and restores `callers --exact` / `unused` behavior for methods reached only through ternary branches. Added unit coverage for ternary continuations, constructor chaining, and nullable return types plus an integration test that verifies `callers --json --exact` sees a ternary call site again. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #175.
- **VB.NET symbol extraction now captures namespaces and implicit-visibility declarations (#166)** — `SymbolExtractor` now indexes `Namespace ... End Namespace` blocks as real `namespace` symbols in VB, makes visibility optional for `Sub`, `Function`, `Class`, `Module`, `Structure`, `Interface`, and `Enum`, and accepts leading modifiers such as `Shared`, `Overrides`, and `Partial` even when no explicit access modifier is present. VB `Property` and `Event` declarations are now indexed as first-class symbols as well, and `VisualBasicEnd` container tracking now recognizes `Namespace` blocks so nested VB symbols retain the correct container metadata. Added regression coverage for namespace extraction, implicit-visibility members and types, leading modifiers, and VB property/event declarations. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #166.
- **SQL symbol extraction now covers temp/materialized objects and stops inventing `class ON` (#173)** — SQL extraction now treats `CREATE TEMP[TEMPORARY] TABLE`, `GLOBAL/LOCAL TEMPORARY TABLE`, `UNLOGGED TABLE`, and `CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW` as class-like symbols; captures `CREATE TYPE`, `CREATE SEQUENCE`, `CREATE DOMAIN`, `CREATE SCHEMA`, and `CREATE EXTENSION`; and classifies `CREATE TYPE ... AS ENUM` as an `enum` plus `CREATE SCHEMA` as a `namespace` and `CREATE EXTENSION` as an `import`. Anonymous `CREATE INDEX ON ...` statements no longer capture the keyword `ON` as a bogus index name, while named and unique indexes still extract normally. Added SQL regression tests and aligned the README / developer SQL capability tables with actual symbol support. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #173.
- **`hotspots` now keeps unique cross-file refs while de-inflating duplicate names (#151)** — `GetSymbolHotspots` now computes name ambiguity from the unscoped language/kind candidate set so `--path` / `--exclude-tests` cannot hide an out-of-scope duplicate and accidentally promote a same-name symbol back to codebase-wide counting. Cross-file grouping now requires an authoritative persisted family key that is scoped to an unambiguous project/root boundary: markerless folders now fall back to their top-level subtree instead of one repo-wide `"."` scope, while markerless root-level files continue sharing `"."` so one-project partial families are not split per file, and directories containing multiple matching project files degrade to narrower subtree/file scopes instead of incorrectly sharing one project scope. Ambiguity and reference counting are now partitioned by symbol language as well, so `--lang csharp` no longer counts Python `Run()` callers and mixed-language same-name definitions no longer suppress otherwise-valid hotspots. Duplicate families only promote to codebase-wide counts when they resolve to one authoritative family or one same-file container family; unrelated same-file containers no longer inherit global counts just because they share a file, and same-file sibling containers no longer borrow each other's ambiguous local refs. Hotspot-family trust now tracks project-marker fingerprints per language instead of through one global marker bit, so unrelated `*.vbproj` / `*.fsproj` changes no longer demote authoritative C# partial-family hotspots, while changed marker classes still leave only their own language degraded until a safe restamp. Reader-side trust now also requires the per-language marker fingerprint metadata to be present, so mixed/upgraded DBs that keep `hotspot_family_version_*` but lose `hotspot_family_marker_fingerprint_*` no longer masquerade as authoritative. The hotspot-family trust version was also bumped for the markerless-scope contract change, so older DBs stamped with repo-wide `"."` fallback automatically degrade until they are reindexed under the new rules. Marker fingerprint collection now follows the same best-effort traversal policy as normal scanning, so unreadable subtrees no longer crash `index` setup or destroy a usable DB on `--rebuild`. Hotspot-family trust reporting now treats any indexed marker-capable language as relevant even when legacy rows have no persisted `family_key`, so legacy/null-`family_key` DBs are explicitly flagged degraded instead of being misreported as authoritative. CLI JSON and MCP `symbol_hotspots` now surface `hotspot_family_ready` plus a degraded reason, human `hotspots` output warns when conservative fallback is active, and CLI help text now states that duplicate-name families may fall back conservatively. The dedicated hotspot-family metadata is cleared at the first real write of CLI/MCP index runs, only restamped on successful completion, and its clear path now tolerates fresh `--rebuild` databases before `codeindex_meta` exists. Partial detection is now case-insensitive, and VB type blocks now expose container ranges, so VB `Partial` families get the same cross-file hotspot behavior as C#. Grouped hotspot rows also reuse a real representative definition row so the reported `path:line` always points at an actual definition. Truly ambiguous duplicate-name families still fall back to conservative in-target file counts. Added regression coverage for out-of-scope duplicate names, unique cross-file callers, same-container overload families, partial-class overload families, markerless root-level partial families, missing marker fingerprints, namespace-separated same-simple containers, Python module duplicates, cross-project duplicate types, cross-project partial families, markerless multi-subtree repos, stale v1 markerless family scopes, VB partial families, grouped-definition jump targets, same-file duplicate-name collapse, ambiguous multi-project directories, mixed legacy/current family-key states, same-file duplicate containers, failed partial refresh demotion, marker-only scope changes, fresh rebuild flows, unreadable marker subtrees, cross-language definition ambiguity, cross-language reference inflation, per-marker trust isolation, and degraded hotspot-family signaling. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSymbolReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbContext.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbWriter.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ConsoleUi.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ConsoleUiTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/IndexCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/LegacySchemaMigrationTests.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolDefinitions.cs`, `README.md`. Closes #151.
- **Modern Node JavaScript/TypeScript extensions are now indexed instead of being silently skipped (#156)** — `FileIndexer` now recognizes `.cjs` and `.mjs` as JavaScript plus `.cts` and `.mts` as TypeScript, which also covers declaration variants such as `.d.cts` and `.d.mts` because detection keys off the final extension. `cdidx languages` / MCP `languages` now surface those extensions, and README examples call out modern Node/dual-publish package coverage explicitly. Added regression tests for direct language detection, file scanning, CLI `languages --json`, and MCP `languages`. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`, `README.md`. Closes #156.

- **Long single-line reference/excerpt payloads are now clamped for AI-friendly query output (#157)** — Added `--max-line-width` to `references`, `find`, `excerpt`, and bundled `inspect` / MCP `analyze_symbol` reference context so minified or single-line generated files no longer dump entire 10 KB+ / 70 KB+ lines into CLI JSON or MCP responses. `excerpt` now also accepts focus hints (`--focus-line`, `--focus-column`, `--focus-length`, plus MCP `focusLine` / `focusColumn` / `focusLength`) so line clamping keeps the requested token visible instead of falling back to a misleading head-only slice; `focusLine` / `focusLength` now explicitly require `focusColumn`, and non-supporting CLI commands reject these excerpt-only controls instead of silently ignoring them. Without focus hints, `excerpt` still clamps long single-line payloads instead of silently returning the full line. Added regression coverage for DB reader, CLI, MCP, and help/completion text. - **Focused excerpt columns now fail closed when they fall outside the target line, and `references` help advertises count mode correctly (#157)** — `excerpt` / MCP `excerpt` now reject `focusColumn` values that exceed the focused line length instead of silently clamping to an unrelated tail fragment, and the defensive reader path also returns no excerpt for impossible focused columns. The CLI/help/doc inventories now include `references --count` again so the supported count-only mode stays discoverable. Added regression coverage for DB reader, CLI, MCP, and help output. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ConsoleUi.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolDefinitions.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ConsoleUiTests.cs`, `README.md`, `CLAUDE.md`. - **Explicit `--db` queries now use persisted project roots instead of leaking the caller's worktree metadata (#152)** — Query-time workspace enrichment for `status`, `map`, and `inspect` now trusts the default `.cdidx/codeindex.db` sibling path for implicit queries without `--db`, so moving or renaming the current repo does not leave stale absolute project roots behind. Explicit `--db` queries instead read `indexed_project_root` from `codeindex_meta` when available instead of inheriting the caller's current working directory. Legacy explicit DBs without stored root metadata now leave `project_root`, `git_head`, and `git_is_dirty` unset until a run against the intended project commits at least one real file delete/update, even when the explicit path itself looks like `.../.cdidx/codeindex.db`; no-op shared-DB updates no longer hijack missing root metadata. Explicit read-only `file:...?...immutable=1` DB URIs keep using the same open semantics for metadata reads, stale unsupported-language references are still purged on no-op updates, and update-mode now demotes readiness before the first real mutation so rollback failures cannot leave stale ready bits marked authoritative. Regression coverage now locks the resolver, enricher, CLI, URI, MCP, shared-DB, stale-ref, rename/move, and failure-path behaviors in place. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/DbPathResolver.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/WorkspaceMetadataEnricher.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbContext.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbWriter.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbPathResolverTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/WorkspaceMetadataEnricherTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/IndexCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/LegacySchemaMigrationTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`. Closes #152.
- **CLI query errors now tell the user what to do next** — Common query-side stderr paths now add actionable hints instead of only stating the failure. Missing query/path arguments point to a concrete next command shape, invalid numeric options now fail closed with `UsageError` instead of printing a warning and running with fallback values, and missing/failed database opens now tell users and AI agents to create or refresh the index before rerunning. Invalid `ParseArgs` inputs such as malformed `--since` values now fail fast, parse-error exits now append a command-specific `Usage:` line plus a rerun hint, value-taking options now reject missing tail values, blank inline values such as `--lang=` or `--db=`, and both recognized and unknown flag-swallow cases, and double-dash literal values must use `--opt=<value>` when they would otherwise look like another option (for example `--path=--json-dir` or `--db=--tmp.db`) with that rule now documented in `--help` and README. The top-level `--help` shortcut now also respects `--name` values, `--completions` now treats missing/option-like/extra arguments as actionable `UsageError`s instead of falling through to generic unknown-command handling, and undocumented `--no-json` overrides are now rejected instead of silently flipping output contracts. Unexpected extra positional arguments are rejected on non-`symbols` commands instead of being silently ignored, `languages` and query commands reject unsupported flags when their canonical usage line does not advertise them, unsupported flags now win over malformed values on commands that do not implement them, `mcp` also rejects invalid/unsupported options before starting the server, commands that do not implement `--since` reject it explicitly instead of silently ignoring the filter, and unsupported-option failures no longer preface the hard error with a misleading “ignored” warning. Shared usage/docs stay aligned with the actual implemented options, including `index --dry-run` and the README option matrix. `validate` also rejects unsupported narrowing flags instead of silently ignoring them. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ArgHelper.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ConsoleUi.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Program.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ArgHelperTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ConsoleUiTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ProgramCliTests.cs`, `README.md`, `TESTING_GUIDE.md`.
- **Trimmed-release CLI `--json` now fails with a dedicated feature-unavailable signal instead of a fake database error (#147)** — Published self-contained builds still cannot serialize CLI `--json` payloads under `PublishTrimmed=true`, but the observable failure is now truthful: the CLI reports `Error: --json is not available on this trimmed build.`, prints a structured-output hint that points users at MCP / human-readable output / the NuGet tool build, and exits with code `4` (`FeatureUnavailable`) instead of misclassifying the problem as exit code `3` (`DatabaseError`). Added entrypoint regression tests that cover both the DB-backed `status --json` path and the pre-DB `index --json` error path, updated the user/developer docs to describe the current limitation accurately, and taught the release workflow to assert the published binary now returns exit code `4` without the old `database error` wording. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Program.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ProgramRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/JsonOutputFailure.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/CommandExitCodes.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ProgramRunnerTests.cs`, `.github/workflows/release.yml`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `CLOUD_BOOTSTRAP_PROMPT.md`, `CLAUDE.md`. Closes #147.
- **Unknown-command suggestions no longer over-match short inputs** — `FindClosestCommand` now uses Damerau-Levenshtein distance with a length-aware threshold so short unknown commands are no longer steered toward unrelated longer commands (for example `fold` no longer suggests `find` just because it is within the old global distance-3 cutoff), while common typos and missing hyphens such as `serach` and `backfillfold` still resolve to the intended command. Added regression coverage for the tighter heuristic. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ConsoleUi.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ConsoleUiTests.cs`.
- **Explicit root paths now bypass descendant skip-dir filters (#153)** — `FileIndexer.ScanFiles()` no longer applies the default skip-directory list to the project root itself, so commands like `cdidx node_modules`, `cdidx vendor`, `cdidx target`, or `cdidx .` from inside those directories no longer silently produce empty indexes. Descendant skip behavior is unchanged, and regression tests now cover explicit roots whose leaf names match `SkipDirs`. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`. Closes #153.
- **Release verify step waits for CDN-propagated download URL and `gh release create` is idempotent** — The `Verify install.sh against the published release` step in `.github/workflows/release.yml` previously called `install.sh` immediately after `gh release create`, which races the GitHub release download CDN. Asset URLs returned 404 for several seconds even though the API listed them, making the v1.10.0 release run fail despite the actual release being healthy. Added a preceding `Wait for release assets to be downloadable` step that polls the public `releases/download/<tag>/CodeIndex-linux-x64.tar.gz` URL with up to ten 5-second retries before the verify step runs. Also made `Create GitHub release` idempotent: when the same-tag release already exists (e.g. on a re-run after a transient verify failure), the step now uploads any missing assets via `gh release upload --clobber` instead of failing with `a release with the same tag name already exists`. Affected: `.github/workflows/release.yml`.
- **`inspect` now anchors bundled context to exact-name definitions first (#124)** — When one definition exactly matches the query but other definitions only overlap by prefix/suffix (for example `LoggerService` vs `ILoggerService`), `inspect` / MCP `analyze_symbol` now choose the exact-name definition as the primary file and nearby-symbol anchor instead of inheriting whichever definition sorted first. This keeps the `File:` header and bundled local context aligned with the intended symbol without hiding the other candidate definitions. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSymbolReader.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #124.
- **Alias-qualified C# explicit interface implementations no longer get blocked by the named-argument guard (#122)** — Tightened the explicit-interface call-site rejection so it only filters named-argument labels when they are followed by a qualified call expression. This preserves the #106 false-positive fix for lines like `isWindows: OperatingSystem.IsWindows()` while allowing valid explicit-interface definitions with alias-qualified return types such as `global::System.String IFoo.Name()` and `Alias::Type IFoo.Create()`. Added extractor-level and DbReader integration coverage for both forms. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`. Closes #122.
- **MCP exact degraded-signal fields now align with CLI JSON naming (#127)** — MCP `structuredContent` now exposes the same snake_case exact degraded-signal fields as CLI JSON: `exact_index_available` and `degraded_reason`. To avoid breaking existing MCP clients, the legacy camelCase keys `exactIndexAvailable` and `degradedReason` remain as backward-compatible aliases for now. Updated docs and regression coverage across exact graph queries, exact symbol queries, and `analyze_symbol`.
